# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

## Your Task

Perfect! I've completed the analysis and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings on graceful shutdown signal handling across all three repositories.

## Summary of Findings

I identified **18 key files** implementing SIGTERM/SIGINT graceful shutdown patterns across the three repositories:

### **kubernetes/kubernetes** (6 files)
- **Signal registration**: `SetupSignalContext()` and `SetupSignalHandler()` in apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go
- **Signals defined**: SIGTERM and SIGINT in signal_posix.go
- **Key pattern**: Two-signal approach - first signal initiates graceful shutdown via context cancellation, second signal forces immediate exit with `os.Exit(1)`
- **Cleanup**: `GracefulStop()` on gRPC servers when context is cancelled

### **grafana/grafana** (9 files)
- **Signal registration**: `listenToSystemSignals()` in commands/cli.go with separate handling for SIGTERM/SIGINT and SIGHUP
- **Graceful shutdown**: 30-second timeout context, explicit `Shutdown()` methods in server.go
- **gRPC shutdown**: `GracefulStop()` with configurable timeout (default 10s), falls back to `Stop()` if timeout exceeded
- **Cleanup ordering**: Background services drain before gRPC server stops
- **Operators**: Individual signal handlers in provisioning and IAM operators

### **prometheus/prometheus** (3 files)
- **Signal registration**: oklog/run group orchestration with term channel
- **Key feature**: **Queue draining** - `DrainOnShutdown` option in notifier to send pending alerts before shutdown
- **Cleanup pattern**: `drainQueue()` processes all queued notifications before stopping
- **Configuration**: `--alertmanager.drain-notification-queue-on-shutdown` flag controls drain behavior
- **Service ordering**: Discovery managers, notifiers, rules managers stop in coordin

calls `Stop()` to force shutdown\\n  - Configuration timeout is defined in `pkg/setting/setting_grpc.go` with default 10 seconds\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- gRPC server drains connections first via dropped alerts\\n  - `drainQueue()` loops through queue calling `sendOneBatch()` until queue is empty\\n- Configuration flag `--alertmanager.drain-notification-queue-on-shutdown` (default true) controls this behavior\\n- `notifier/manager.go` Run method returns only after all pending notifications are drained\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- Discovery managers stop first (notification and scrape)\\n- Notifier manager stops with queue draining\\n- Rule manager stops\\n- Web handler stops\\n- Each service's Stop() function is called in reverse order, allowing earlier services to drain timeout context\\n   - Prometheus: Service group orchestration with drain functionality\\n4. **Timeout Protection:** Bounded shutdown time prevents indefinite hangs\\n   - Kubernetes: Second signal forces exit\\n   - Grafana: Explicit 30-second timeout (or service-specific like 10s for gRPC)\\n   - Prometheus: Service dependencies ensure cleanup completes or forces stop\\n5. **Drain Before
